    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1242090-i-m-looking-for-a-girl-captured-by">I&#39;m looking for a &quot;girl captured by indians&quot; book that I read about 30 years ago, so this book would probably be too new. Unfortunately, only one thing I can remember specifically: After the girl was captured, bear grease was put in her hair to prevent parasites. Does anyone know of a book from this genre with the bear greased hair? I have read Catherine Troxell Gonzales&#39; version and it wasn&#39;t there.</a>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68228741" />
    <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books"><img alt="Allison (The Allure of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1247775031p2/1637878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68228741?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison (The Allure of Books)" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books">Allison (The Allure of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68228741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13636853179779190827">This book was recommended by a good friend of mine, and she hasn't steered me wrong yet. This book will break your heart. First it will make you sick, then make you mad, then you will fall in love...then you will repeatedly feel like you've been run over by tanks. For the past three days, I have been hard put to set this down, and I haven't been able to stop thinking about it. <br/><br/>It was kinda surreal reading it, because the story of Quanah Parker is pretty well known to me, I learned about him in v</span>
  <span id="freeText13636853179779190827" style="display:none">This book was recommended by a good friend of mine, and she hasn't steered me wrong yet. This book will break your heart. First it will make you sick, then make you mad, then you will fall in love...then you will repeatedly feel like you've been run over by tanks. For the past three days, I have been hard put to set this down, and I haven't been able to stop thinking about it. <br /><br />It was kinda surreal reading it, because the story of Quanah Parker is pretty well known to me, I learned about him in various Oklahoma history classes growing up, and the mall I grew up going to is even in the city Cynthia Ann and Quanah are buried, and the mall is on the Quanah Parker by-pass.<br /><br />Going into a book about the Indians' dying way of live will of course be sad, but the utter hopelessness and heartbreak of this ending left me upset and even vaguely unsatisfied. I'm not saying that as a fault of the book-it is what actually happened.<br /><br />Anyway, even after having my heart broken at the end...I have to say it was worth it, this is a BEAUTIFULLY written story, and I will undoubtedly be picking it up again someday.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13636853179779190827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer46723974&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer46723974" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"

<span id="freeTextContainer12392011732172220359">Thought this was a romance, but it most definitely is NOT. <br/><br/>The beginning depicts, in graphic detail, a large group of American Indians attacking a Fort. Gang raping, scalping, killing, trampling kids with horses for fun, etc. The few that were unfortunate enough to be taken captive are then repeatedly gang raped, burned and abused. <br/><br/>Cynthia was 9 years old when she was taken as a captive by Wanderer who was 16. She was almost raped, but Wanderer prevented it. The author did not come right out and</span>
  <span id="freeText12392011732172220359" style="display:none">Thought this was a romance, but it most definitely is NOT. <br /><br />The beginning depicts, in graphic detail, a large group of American Indians attacking a Fort. Gang raping, scalping, killing, trampling kids with horses for fun, etc. The few that were unfortunate enough to be taken captive are then repeatedly gang raped, burned and abused. <br /><br />Cynthia was 9 years old when she was taken as a captive by Wanderer who was 16. She was almost raped, but Wanderer prevented it. The author did not come right out and say this, but Wanderer and the others that Cynthia continues to live with, participated in the continued nightly rapes of her Aunt--who was pregnant and nursing a child. <br /><br />The book goes into excruciating detail of the Indian way of life. Endless pages of narration and mind-numbing detail of how to skin a deer, how to use a deer body part for a sack for honey, how to get honey out of a bee hive, how to unpack camp, etc. <br /><br />I just couldn't take it anymore and once I learned there was no HEA and what would happen at the end of this book, I lost all interest in continuing. </span>

<div id="review_57326764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57326764" />
    <a title="Annette2009" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2353991-annette2009"><img alt="Annette2009" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265071129p2/2353991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57326764?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annette2009" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annette2009" href="/user/show/2353991-annette2009">Annette2009</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2353991-annette2009?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57326764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14196544487952450385">A CAPTIVATING, HAUNTING GLIMPSE INTO TEXAS HISTORY<br/><br/>Many of the paperback covers make this book look like a cheesy western romance novel. Do not be fooled! Ride the Wind is based on the true story of Cynthia Ann Parker, who was kidnapped in 1836 during a brutal raid by the Comanche Indians, then adopted and raised by the tribe. I was stunned by my change in perspective – at the beginning, I was horrified by the savagery of the Indians; by the end, I was furious with the savagery and ignorance of t</span>
  <span id="freeText14196544487952450385" style="display:none">A CAPTIVATING, HAUNTING GLIMPSE INTO TEXAS HISTORY<br /><br />Many of the paperback covers make this book look like a cheesy western romance novel. Do not be fooled! Ride the Wind is based on the true story of Cynthia Ann Parker, who was kidnapped in 1836 during a brutal raid by the Comanche Indians, then adopted and raised by the tribe. I was stunned by my change in perspective – at the beginning, I was horrified by the savagery of the Indians; by the end, I was furious with the savagery and ignorance of the Whites. Cynthia, renamed “Naduah,” (sometimes translated as “keeps warm with us”), is assimilated completely into the tribe, marrying a respected warrior and eventually giving birth to Quanah Parker, the last free war chief of the Comanches. The novel sticks with the true story, and it ends in heartbreak, but it is truly a captivating, haunting glimpse into Texas history. It made the “best-loved books” list for both myself and my 97-year-old grandmother, and will be a favorite for readers who love adventure, history, romance, and Comanche Indian culture. Bonus: you can visit Old Fort Parker near Mexia, an authentic recreation of the original frontier settlement, and Palo Duro Canyon, the “Grand Canyon of Texas” so memorably described in the last chapters of the book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14196544487952450385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3101810809801583444"><br/>"Nacona, Wanderer, my brother, I wish the these white people would come west so we could raid them all the time. They have such wonderful things, and they're soft like newborn pups. I may spend ore time here in the east".<br/><br/><br/>Ride the Wind by Lucia St. Clair Robson <br/><br/><br/>As someone with an interest in Native American History I liked reading this story about Cynthia Anne Parker. It made me angry though and not at Native Americans, at OUR government. I felt almost embarrassed on her behalf.<br/><br/>This was a really </span>
  <span id="freeText3101810809801583444" style="display:none"><br />"Nacona, Wanderer, my brother, I wish the these white people would come west so we could raid them all the time. They have such wonderful things, and they're soft like newborn pups. I may spend ore time here in the east".<br /><br /><br />Ride the Wind by Lucia St. Clair Robson <br /><br /><br />As someone with an interest in Native American History I liked reading this story about Cynthia Anne Parker. It made me angry though and not at Native Americans, at OUR government. I felt almost embarrassed on her behalf.<br /><br />This was a really long book and there's alot of violence in it, you have been warned. I did have to skim over some parts of it. But the book taught me alot..which is what great books do. I looked up Cynthia's story after reading this book. Then I got mad all over again.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />This is really just a comment but.. I wish her story had had a happier ending. It was painful.<br /><br />A few years ago, I had the opportunity to see the "trail of tears" which also made me outraged. I can remember, as a child, loving Native American History and wanting to live free as they did. This book really is superb and like many others have wondered I do not get why it has not been turned into a movie(although with Hollywood being involved, who knows how it would turn out?) <br /><br />But this was a great story and my hat's off to the author as I read the story of how she came to write this as well. Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_881261006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/881261006" />
    <a title="Lisazj1" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5816343-lisazj1"><img alt="Lisazj1" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337769434p2/5816343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/881261006?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisazj1" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisazj1" href="/user/show/5816343-lisazj1">Lisazj1</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=real-book-shelf">real-book-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=oh-my-heart">oh-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=western-wilderness-frontier">western-wilderness-frontier</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5816343-lisazj1?shelf=recommend-forever">recommend-forever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer881261006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12421497472882805186">I'm a big book loaner. Every time I read something I loved, my first impulse is to give it to someone else immediately, "here, <i>read</i> this!". And a lot of times, I never get that book back. If I <i>really</i> loved it, I go and buy it again, so I still have a copy. Consequently, I have owned 7 copies of this book (yeah, I am dumb, because I kept loaning it out). The last time I bought it, I was told it was out of print, so I held on to that copy.<br/><br/>I've always been interested in Native American history, and</span>
  <span id="freeText12421497472882805186" style="display:none">I'm a big book loaner. Every time I read something I loved, my first impulse is to give it to someone else immediately, "here, <i>read</i> this!". And a lot of times, I never get that book back. If I <i>really</i> loved it, I go and buy it again, so I still have a copy. Consequently, I have owned 7 copies of this book (yeah, I am dumb, because I kept loaning it out). The last time I bought it, I was told it was out of print, so I held on to that copy.<br /><br />I've always been interested in Native American history, and I remember how that interest fired when I read the back cover of this. This is a fictional story based on factual events. Cynthia Ann Parker was 9 years old when she &amp; her brother were captured by Comanches in a raid and later adopted into their tribe. Cynthia (later Naduah) grew up to marry one of the Comanche's fiercest chiefs, Nocona. Her son Quanah Parker grew up to be the last free Comanche war chief. Much of what Ms St. Clair Robson wrote of their lives was taken from published interviews with Quanah Parker, who by all accounts was quite charming and social and loved to talk about his mother.<br /><br />I think I was just a few years out of high school when I first read this, yet I can tell you everything that happened here. I remember all the names and what they mean. I remember the battles, nights laughing under the moon, the sickness, conversations, Pah-mo the gazelle, betrayals, and deaths. The hatred, tenderness, sorrow, love, violence and stunning brutality. Everything. I've read this several times over the years, but there always comes the point where I just can't read on, and eventually I stopped re-reading. *there's your warning that there is no friggin' HEA*<br /><br />If there is anything that I can think of that some might not enjoy, it's the detail of their day-to-day life, as it could maybe sometimes be a bit tedious, depending on how interested you were in the first place but I was always fascinated.<br /><br />Might not be a book for everyone but it's one of the most wrenching, memorable stories I've ever read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12421497472882805186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=rape">rape</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=western">western</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1517217385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4177935270259873100"><br/>3.5<br/><br/>There is a great deal of details involving the lives and customs of the plains Indians in this version of the Cynthia Anne Parker story. This was a very romanticized depiction, but there are some extremely brutal scenes throughout the story. Aside from the gushy romance, this novel was told with great adventure and detail. Good for details on the lives of the Native Americans, good for an adventurous story, not so good for the facts about the life of Cynthia Anne Parker. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_29342714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29342714" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29342714?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29342714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7850988605370470387">This book is beautiful, uplifting, shocking, hopeful, desolate, almost any emotion possible to feel will be aroused. St. Clair Robson takes the kidnapping of a young plainsgirl, and tells the story that will live in your heart years after reading it. The white child who grows to marry a chief. Who bears the very last free Comanche chief in America. Is she still white?<br/><br/>She pulls no punches. She shows us the brutalities with which the Indians were treated, but on the other side of the coin, in the </span>
  <span id="freeText7850988605370470387" style="display:none">This book is beautiful, uplifting, shocking, hopeful, desolate, almost any emotion possible to feel will be aroused. St. Clair Robson takes the kidnapping of a young plainsgirl, and tells the story that will live in your heart years after reading it. The white child who grows to marry a chief. Who bears the very last free Comanche chief in America. Is she still white?<br /><br />She pulls no punches. She shows us the brutalities with which the Indians were treated, but on the other side of the coin, in the most fair portrayal I have seen, she shows us how brutal they could be. Not only to their enemies, but to each other.<br /><br />She teaches you how harmoniously the Original Americans lived with the land. How they used every resource available to them and wasted nothing. They were so ahead of where we, as country, now want to be. They understood the value of the land, the animals, the human spirit. They valued their children as treasures instilled with their future.<br /><br />The end of the book is brutal. Not physically, but it brings up the question: At what point is a kidnapping victim no longer a victim? At what point can we be left to our own decisions, regardless of race, creed, beliefs? Are some not good or intelligent enough to know what's best for themselves? Who gets to decide where someone belongs? Where they are most needed, wanted, regardless of their personal wishes?<br /><br />I cry each time I come to the end. How could you not?</span>
  <a data-text-id="7850988605370470387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_63851830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63851830" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/772358-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368280030p2/772358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63851830?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/772358-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63851830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6186722789944201656">If you are looking for a book about what it would be like to live with Indians, this is the book. It is based on the true story of a 9 year old white girl that was captured by Indians. The story line is definitely fictional though, as there is no written account from Cynthia Anne, the white girl, only that information from her white relatives and her oldest son, Quanah, the last free Indian Chief. She was raised by a Comanche Indian family and married an Indian chief and had three children with </span>
  <span id="freeText6186722789944201656" style="display:none">If you are looking for a book about what it would be like to live with Indians, this is the book. It is based on the true story of a 9 year old white girl that was captured by Indians. The story line is definitely fictional though, as there is no written account from Cynthia Anne, the white girl, only that information from her white relatives and her oldest son, Quanah, the last free Indian Chief. She was raised by a Comanche Indian family and married an Indian chief and had three children with him. She lived with them for 24 years before she was discovered and returned to her family. It was a really interesting book, covered many events in the history of the Indians in the mid to late 1800's, and definitely portrayed the good and the bad. It made me feel sympathy for the plight of the Indians... and not so much for the whites. I found myself rooting for the Indians despite the terrible things they often did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6186722789944201656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_124939497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124939497" />
    <a title="Tamara Silver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/821163-tamara-silver"><img alt="Tamara Silver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1235408346p2/821163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124939497?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tamara Silver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tamara Silver" href="/user/show/821163-tamara-silver">Tamara Silver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124939497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2552916942910635659">The cheesy cover had me very skeptical about this book, but I think this is a book that is going to stay with me for years and years. Yes, there is better writing, but man oh man, what a story! I learned about Native Americans, the Texas Rangers, and Westward Expansion, in a way that I never learned in school. Learned about daily life, motivations, and how the Indians and settlers impacted each other. The book doesn't whitewash Indian attrocities, you do not get a trite, "at-one-with-nature" vie</span>
  <span id="freeText2552916942910635659" style="display:none">The cheesy cover had me very skeptical about this book, but I think this is a book that is going to stay with me for years and years. Yes, there is better writing, but man oh man, what a story! I learned about Native Americans, the Texas Rangers, and Westward Expansion, in a way that I never learned in school. Learned about daily life, motivations, and how the Indians and settlers impacted each other. The book doesn't whitewash Indian attrocities, you do not get a trite, "at-one-with-nature" view of the Native Americans. Yet even after reading about cruel and twisted acts by the Indians I feel much more empathetic to what happened to them. Oh, and it is based on a true story! A great work of historical fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2552916942910635659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I loved the hero, Nocona, so much I even named my next dog after him :)<br/><br/>A warning though, this book is absolutely wrenching and not for the faint of heart.               >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2572224173495879078">Still one of my all time favorite books! Based on historical events, this is a story of Cynthia Ann Parker’s abduction and assimilation into the lives of the Comanches that kidnapped her. It outlines the gradual fall of the people. Beautiful, yet haunting. The incredible sadness will stay with you for months, if not years.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1827161058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1827161058" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1827161058?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/17957823-erin">Erin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1827161058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12048322287412479230">Despite the deceiving cover that makes it look like a cheap romance, Ride the Wind shares the story of a young girl who is adopted into a Native American tribe. As she grows, the American government's presence becomes even more prominent and threatens the traditional culture and way of life for her adopted family.<br/><br/> I felt that Lucia St.Clair Robson really wanted readers to get a feeling for 19th century life, the dangers faced by early settlers, the life of the Native Americans etc. The good and </span>
  <span id="freeText12048322287412479230" style="display:none">Despite the deceiving cover that makes it look like a cheap romance, Ride the Wind shares the story of a young girl who is adopted into a Native American tribe. As she grows, the American government's presence becomes even more prominent and threatens the traditional culture and way of life for her adopted family.<br /><br /> I felt that Lucia St.Clair Robson really wanted readers to get a feeling for 19th century life, the dangers faced by early settlers, the life of the Native Americans etc. The good and the bad. Some readers might find the graphic violence, including rape and torture, to be too much to stomach. Speaking plainly, I was more bogged down by the description of menial tasks and the shifting of viewpoints of characters within chapters that slowed the pacing of the story.<br /><br />A thought out story, but one which I wouldn't revisit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12048322287412479230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2160669156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2160669156" />
    <a title="Herman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40706083-herman"><img alt="Herman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596816409p2/40706083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2160669156?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Herman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Herman" href="/user/show/40706083-herman">Herman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=excellent-history-books">excellent-history-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=women-who-kick-ass-and-take-names">women-who-kick-ass-and-take-names</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=book-club-recommendations">book-club-recommendations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=native-american">native-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=my-top-rated-recommend-this-book">my-top-rated-recommend-this-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2160669156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8558370032958860071">I read <a>The Red Heart</a> by James Alexander Thom, and I thought that was the best written account of a white adopted by native’s that I had ever read now I’m not so sure, this was a very moving and well written story, and while it was rather long it was well worth my time. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553800851i/27280615._SY540_.jpg' width='242' height='300' alt='Nautdah' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>An excellent account of Nautdah (Cynthia Ann Parker ) who lived with “The People” for 24 years a story full of sadness and drama and love and some inaccuracies too, although not as many as can be found in any Google search of this</span>
  <span id="freeText8558370032958860071" style="display:none">I read <a>The Red Heart</a> by James Alexander Thom, and I thought that was the best written account of a white adopted by native’s that I had ever read now I’m not so sure, this was a very moving and well written story, and while it was rather long it was well worth my time. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553800851i/27280615._SY540_.jpg" width="242" height="300" alt="Nautdah" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>An excellent account of Nautdah (Cynthia Ann Parker ) who lived with “The People” for 24 years a story full of sadness and drama and love and some inaccuracies too, although not as many as can be found in any Google search of this subject I was excited to read this for I knew much about this story but I hadn’t as yet read a full accounting of Cynthia Parker’s life, nor that of her famous son Quanah Parker. I know the work of this author Lucia St. Clair Robson from having read her books before, and knew she did an excellent job of research as well as lending to her stories a clear women’s viewpoint which is not often heard in fictional (His Story) I also feel the author, in a strange way, seems to me to be something of a ghost-whisper able to bring alive people from the past who left no written records and who’s lives come down to us mostly from tales told from their white enemies, but under her direction they live they grow and they survive in very complex and intelligently written ways. This is a moving account of the changes brought to the Plains Indians by the advent of white society a legacy of love and hate of death and survival. A very good story five stars for this one well worth the month long effort it took to finish it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8558370032958860071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226242422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18009862771547397172">Excellent book on the life of Cynthia Ann Parker and the last days of the free Comanche. This is a true story with a lot of information added on the daily lives of the Comanche.<br/><br/>This subject is close to my heart since Cynthia Ann (Naduah is her Comanche name) is one of my ancestors. However, that's not what makes this such a great book. St. Clair Robson is a wonderful storyteller.   <span id="freeText18009862771547397172" style="display:none">Excellent book on the life of Cynthia Ann Parker and the last days of the free Comanche. This is a true story with a lot of information added on the daily lives of the Comanche.<br /><br />This subject is close to my heart since Cynthia Ann (Naduah is her Comanche name) is one of my ancestors. However, that's not what makes this such a great book. St. Clair Robson is a wonderful storyteller. She is able to weave the true events of Cynthia Ann's life, and the daily details of the lives of the Comanche into a book that keeps the reader engaged and interested throughout the entire 600 pages. That's not an easy feat.<br /><br />I would recommend this book for those interested in Native American culture, historical novel readers, Texas and/or the Old west history lovers and those who like very sweet love stories.</span>

<div id="review_1038786218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1038786218" />
    <a title=" Olivermagnus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9919989-olivermagnus"><img alt=" Olivermagnus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483717985p2/9919989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1038786218?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Olivermagnus" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Olivermagnus" href="/user/show/9919989-olivermagnus"> Olivermagnus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12375904-ride-the-wind">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9919989-olivermagnus?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9919989-olivermagnus?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9919989-olivermagnus?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9919989-olivermagnus?shelf=poll">poll</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038786218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13847059446775919542">What a great read this book turned out to be! It's the historical fiction retelling of the story of Cynthia Ann Parker, kidnapped at the age of nine by a Comanche war band who massacred her family’s settlement in Texas. She was adopted by the Comanche and lived with them for 24 years, eventually marrying a Comanche chieftain and having three children with him, including the last free Comanche chief Quanah Parker. When she was 34, she was finally "rescued" by the Texas Rangers and returned to her</span>
  <span id="freeText13847059446775919542" style="display:none">What a great read this book turned out to be! It's the historical fiction retelling of the story of Cynthia Ann Parker, kidnapped at the age of nine by a Comanche war band who massacred her family’s settlement in Texas. She was adopted by the Comanche and lived with them for 24 years, eventually marrying a Comanche chieftain and having three children with him, including the last free Comanche chief Quanah Parker. When she was 34, she was finally "rescued" by the Texas Rangers and returned to her white family. She spent the remaining years of her life in lonely misery, refusing to adjust to life in white society. The author appears to have thoroughly researched the conflict between the Comanche tribe and the Texans. I appreciated the way she told both sides of the story and the way Cynthia Ann Parker (Naduah in Comanche) is portrayed. In reality she never told anyone about her life among the Comanche but based on the stories from her son, Quanah Parker, I would like to think that the author's version was how it happened.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book very much but it is very difficult to read in places. It's often violent, very shocking reading, and is not for the faint of heart. Some of the atrocities were very difficult to read through especially the deaths of the children and babies. They die from disease and from the elements but many of them are brutally tortured and murdered. <br /><br />This is a wonderfully written and readable book. The author does a great job of describing the culture and time period. In many ways it is a heartbreaking book that documents a time and way of life that is gone forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13847059446775919542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5143957289845299104">This book leaves me in a quandary. It was so well written, and yet parts were SO BORING. And parts were amazing, but some parts were not. <br/><br/>I thought the character development of everyone was so well done it was ridiculous. As I read the book I became one of the People and I fell in love with the characters. When they died, parts of me died with them. <br/><br/>I thought the beginning was a little much. It was ridiculously graphic and could have been... not that graphic. Also, Rachel Plummer didn't need to </span>
  <span id="freeText5143957289845299104" style="display:none">This book leaves me in a quandary. It was so well written, and yet parts were SO BORING. And parts were amazing, but some parts were not. <br /><br />I thought the character development of everyone was so well done it was ridiculous. As I read the book I became one of the People and I fell in love with the characters. When they died, parts of me died with them. <br /><br />I thought the beginning was a little much. It was ridiculously graphic and could have been... not that graphic. Also, Rachel Plummer didn't need to keep making reappearances. That was weird and unnecessary. The sex and violence were not my favorite. It wasn't necessarily gratuitous sex as it was extremely detailed. Just as the violence was pretty detailed. <br /><br />Everything else was fascinating. The culture and the people and the story line. I did get pretty bored during the Texan soldier bits. I don't know why those were ever necessary because they were drop dead boring. The book could have been at least 100 pages shorter if we didn't have to read about random hairy soldier guys. <br /><br />Best love story ever. Well, how about best love story with the weirdest beginning ever. Yeah, that's more accurate. <br /><br />I don't know. I couldn't stop thinking about the book, I couldn't put it down but I don't think I'll ever read it again. It was a little much for me. But I'm glad I read it once. <br /><br />(Also what the heck happened to Pecan?!)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5143957289845299104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Amy (mrsAmy#s)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy (mrsAmy#s)" href="/user/show/1544042-amy-mrsamy-s">Amy (mrsAmy#s)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65143295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6463906715971747962">I'm a little torn on this book between 3 and 4 stars. Part of me LOVED it. I'm a fan of historical fiction and this story about the last few decades of the "free" Comanches is something I was unfamiliar with. The plot was quite fascinating and I liked the Wanderer/Nadua love story.<br/><br/>On the other hand, the first half of the book was markedly better than the second half. The second half was full of cliches,e.g., "We're in love and our two awesome horses had TWINS that look just like their parents". </span>
  <span id="freeText6463906715971747962" style="display:none">I'm a little torn on this book between 3 and 4 stars. Part of me LOVED it. I'm a fan of historical fiction and this story about the last few decades of the "free" Comanches is something I was unfamiliar with. The plot was quite fascinating and I liked the Wanderer/Nadua love story.<br /><br />On the other hand, the first half of the book was markedly better than the second half. The second half was full of cliches,e.g., "We're in love and our two awesome horses had TWINS that look just like their parents". Cheesy. And certain things were totally rushed (one of the main character's friend is killed towards the end with hardly a mention). It also seemed to move a lot slower for me in the second half.<br /><br />Something I'm not sure about- the violence in this book. I'm not sure when I last read something with such potent images of rape, torture, killing. Now, don't get me wrong- I think these portrayals were necessary in the context of the story, but... yowza. Makes me glad I didn't live in Texas back then!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6463906715971747962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15798905878631767543">This book continues to remain one of my favorite books of all time. This is not a romance, it's one of one several historical fiction books written by this author that feature real people and real stories. Her research and portrayal of the Comanche is spot on. It's brutal and loving all at the same time. Robson doesn't sugar coat their lifestyle or the things they did, at the same time she shows their heart. It's a historical fiction because Cynthia Anne never spoke of her life. She was captured</span>
  <span id="freeText15798905878631767543" style="display:none">This book continues to remain one of my favorite books of all time. This is not a romance, it's one of one several historical fiction books written by this author that feature real people and real stories. Her research and portrayal of the Comanche is spot on. It's brutal and loving all at the same time. Robson doesn't sugar coat their lifestyle or the things they did, at the same time she shows their heart. It's a historical fiction because Cynthia Anne never spoke of her life. She was captured when she was 9, she spent 24 years with the Comanche and died within a few years of being rescued. This book has no happy ending, it's an unflinching look at the last years off their freedom and one white woman who became one of them so thoroughly she could not and would not adapt back to her original culture.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15798905878631767543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_940240891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940240891" />
    <a title="Beccalarge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125138-beccalarge"><img alt="Beccalarge" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/940240891?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beccalarge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beccalarge" href="/user/show/1125138-beccalarge">Beccalarge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer940240891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13889286242647569824">It's been a while since I have given 5 stars, but this book is incredible and just might be a new favorite. My mom and sister have been telling me for a while to read it, but to be honest, the cover sort of put me off. When I finally cracked it open and started reading I COULD NOT put it down....it was like finding a treasure!<br/><br/>This book is worth reading for the history alone. It's the true story of young girl who was captured by the Comanche Indians at 9 years old. I have always loved reading abo</span>
  <span id="freeText13889286242647569824" style="display:none">It's been a while since I have given 5 stars, but this book is incredible and just might be a new favorite. My mom and sister have been telling me for a while to read it, but to be honest, the cover sort of put me off. When I finally cracked it open and started reading I COULD NOT put it down....it was like finding a treasure!<br /><br />This book is worth reading for the history alone. It's the true story of young girl who was captured by the Comanche Indians at 9 years old. I have always loved reading about the Native Americans and this is one of THE BEST I have ever read. I loved learning about the day to day lives of the People, and found that this book was acurate on so many levels. I knew that the story was true, but I was blown away by the details of the different tribes, the differences in raiding, hunting, moving, eating, even the way they abused and mutilated their captives (and themselves while grieving). <br /><br />I did a lot my own research while reading, because although I know the author obviously took liberty with the characters and even some of the timing of events, I really wanted to know how deep the fiction went. From what I could find, this is an extremely accurate account of events. Even Cynthia Ann, the young captive who quickly assimilates into the tribe and finds herself not only happy, but thriving among the people is supported by many accounts. It is true that she was deeply in love with the man she marries, the Chief of the Naconi band (he was one of the leaders of the raid at Parker's Fort where she was captured). Chief Nacona was every bit the great warrior and leader that he is in the book, and it is true that he did not take any other wives after Cynthia, something unheard of for a chief. It is also true that Cynthia was a healer in the tribe and was greatly respected. She always rode at the front alongside her husband and carried his lance and shield (a sign not only of her place but of her husbands love and respect for her).<br /><br />This book is not for the faint of heart however....and I have to warn you...it is GRAPHIC. This is the real story and the author does not spare the details of war or of life. I found myself appalled at times, the brutality of the Indians was hard to read and the way they mutilated their captives was more than I could take. And yet I loved them and felt sorry for them when the White men took their lands and the life they had known. I cried when the white buffalo hunters came along, killing off the buffalo in order to obtain their hides, and then leaving the meat to rot. It felt so wrong knowing that the Indians used every inch of the animals they killed, even the massive buffalo, leaving nothing behind (not even bones or brain), and knowing that without buffalo to hunt the Indians would not survive. <br /><br />This is a great book. For it's history and for the story surrounding it. Beautifully written with so many details and beautiful descriptions. The characters felt so real to me, I loved them, cried with them and even missed them when I finished the book. <br /><br />I think everyone should read this book, should know the story Comanche Indians. And this leads me to the only real issue I have with the book.....it's too graphic to recommend. I could handle the bloody war details and for the most part felt that their authenticity was important (although wished at times the author would have been brief), but there are a couple of sex scenes that are just too graphic for young readers (and even for me). And for that reason I feel like I can't recomend it to others without a strong warning. <br /><br />But it really is my new FAVORITE. And I will read it again...and again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13889286242647569824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82439732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82439732" />
    <a title="Alexis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/783473-alexis"><img alt="Alexis" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82439732?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexis" href="/user/show/783473-alexis">Alexis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/783473-alexis?shelf=interesting">interesting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82439732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15899334780954778072">Okay, so the things I liked about this book outweigh the things I didn't...I think. Thats why I gave it 4 stars. That and I'm patting myself on the back for finishing. I really enjoyed that this book was set in Texas, much of it where I'm from in the Panhandle. Loved thinking about what this area looked like not even 2 centuries ago. Cynthia Ann Parker, or Naduah, is absolutely facinating. I can totally understand why her life and death caused such a stir, even to this day. The whole White Man/I</span>
  <span id="freeText15899334780954778072" style="display:none">Okay, so the things I liked about this book outweigh the things I didn't...I think. Thats why I gave it 4 stars. That and I'm patting myself on the back for finishing. I really enjoyed that this book was set in Texas, much of it where I'm from in the Panhandle. Loved thinking about what this area looked like not even 2 centuries ago. Cynthia Ann Parker, or Naduah, is absolutely facinating. I can totally understand why her life and death caused such a stir, even to this day. The whole White Man/Indian issue is so interesting to think about. What if things had just been a little bit different? Anyway, I love historical fiction because it so brings history to life. Makes you view events from the perspective of the people who may have actually experienced it. I'm ashamed to say I live about a stones throw away from Adobe Walls and have never visited. I shall remedy that!<br /><br />So for the things I did not enjoy. It was just too dang long! I think the author WAY over did certain topics. She was obviously very throrough, but there's only so much I want to know about tracking someone's hoof prints or finding water in what looks like a desert. Or what they may have eaten at EVERY single meal! It was also quick to turn trashy romance novel-ish. And her flowery descriptions of landscape would go ON and ON! I was relieved to find out she is from Maryland. She would write scenarios that I was like, there is NO WAY that happend in Texas! At one point Naduah's family is travelling through a blizzard right after a huge prairie fire...around Austin! When was the last time there was a blizzard OR a prairie in the hill country?? Umm, never! The Panhandle, maybe. But then another time the temperatures at Palo Duro Canyon are supposed to be -25 degrees. Now, we just came through a bitter cold spell, and maybe the wind chill got that cold, but definitely not the temp!<br /><br />So anyway, the good outweighed the bad. I would reccommend this book to anyone from Texas, especially the Panhandle, hill country or around Nocona or with ties to the Commanche tribe. Interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15899334780954778072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11006902285454979413">I read this book years ago, then couldn't find it. I recently found a copy, but upon re-reading it I found that it depressed me to read the plight of the American Indian and the injustices done to them and their culture. I feel that this book is a close to life depiction of what happened to their culture and the angst between them and white people. If your are looking for a true to life story (this is a fictional depiction of a true life story) of Comanche Indians and the loss of their culture y</span>
  <span id="freeText11006902285454979413" style="display:none">I read this book years ago, then couldn't find it. I recently found a copy, but upon re-reading it I found that it depressed me to read the plight of the American Indian and the injustices done to them and their culture. I feel that this book is a close to life depiction of what happened to their culture and the angst between them and white people. If your are looking for a true to life story (this is a fictional depiction of a true life story) of Comanche Indians and the loss of their culture you must read this book. If you want the fairy tale version you might want to pick a different one. <br /><br />I give this book 5 out of 5 stars.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2882462780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15490385020267016796">Amazing. Took me too long to read this because I had to put it down when the semester started in the fall due to so much homework :( I read 75% before the semester started and I would have finished it right away if it wasn't for school because this book was incredible. Some parts were definitely hard to read, like the torture scenes with Rachel and Cruelest One. It is really difficult for me to read books or watch any movies with torture. It was also difficult for me to understand the way the Co</span>
  <span id="freeText15490385020267016796" style="display:none">Amazing. Took me too long to read this because I had to put it down when the semester started in the fall due to so much homework :( I read 75% before the semester started and I would have finished it right away if it wasn't for school because this book was incredible. Some parts were definitely hard to read, like the torture scenes with Rachel and Cruelest One. It is really difficult for me to read books or watch any movies with torture. It was also difficult for me to understand the way the Comanches and other tribes took in young white kids to raise as their own but tortured and mutilated other white settlers, including unwanted children and women.<br /><br />Although these parts were hard to understand and made me wonder why so much brutality was necessary, I always reminded myself that it was the white settlers who started war with Native Americans. In fact, Native Americans did not even believe in owning land, so they could not understand the concept of buying land and so many other problems the settlers brought with them. The settlers killed so many Native Americans for no reason at all but to own land. <br /><br />This book shows their struggles in a different and more personal than is usually taught. It was touching and inspiring to learn how the Comanches lived off the land, treated illness and how they raised their families. I loved Naduah and Wanderer's relationship, especially the parts leading up to them getting together. Her admiration for him and his protection over her was so sweet.<br /><br />The book also displays the diseases white settlers brought over a long period of time. We all have learned in our textbooks about how the Europeans brought over smallpox, cholera, diphtheria and more but it was different to read it in a novel. It was devastating to see these illnesses affect main characters. Moreover, it was shocking to learn that despite the value Native Americans had on family, the diseases that were brought over made them fear members of their families and leave suspicious members behind. Although it was heartbreaking, this book was beautiful and an instant favorite for me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15490385020267016796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4602399311084404812">Lucia St. Clair Robson has been a Peace Corps Volunteer, a teacher and a librarian. Her first historical novel, RIDE THE WIND, appeared on the New York Times best seller list, and in 1983 received the Golden Spur Award from the Western Writers of America. Since then she has written seven more novels set in a variety of times and places. Kirkus Reviews wrote, "Few novelists working today have a bet</span>
  <span id="freeText4602399311084404812" style="display:none">Lucia St. Clair Robson has been a Peace Corps Volunteer, a teacher and a librarian. Her first historical novel, RIDE THE WIND, appeared on the New York Times best seller list, and in 1983 received the Golden Spur Award from the Western Writers of America. Since then she has written seven more novels set in a variety of times and places. Kirkus Reviews wrote, "Few novelists working today have a better grasp of early American history than Robson.""</span>
